COMMITTEE REPORTS:  
 
CR 25-1 Recommending FIRST READING of Bill 7, CD1 (2025), to amend the 
Fiscal Year 2025 Budget by: 1) amending Section 2, Estimated Revenues, by 
increasing Carryover/Savings from the General Fund by $1,500,000; 2) 
amending Section 3.B.12.c.(2), Office of the Mayo r, Economic Development 
Program, Grants and disbursements for business development and technology, 
by adding a new appropriation, entitled "Festivals of Aloha, Inc. for the 2025 
Maui County Fair, " in the amount of $1,500,000; and 3) adjusting the totals 
accordingly.

MS. MATTHEWS. >> GOOD MORNING, CHAIR AND THANK YOU FOR THAT. I HAVE SUCH 
HIGH ESTEEM FOR KUMU KAMAKA HERNANDEZ IN HAWAI'I AND AROUND THE WORLD I 
WANTED TO THANK THE COUNCIL FOR HONORING BLACK HISTORY MONTH HERE TODAY. 
BLACK HISTORY MONTH HOLDS A VERY SPECIAL PLACE FOR ME. MY MOM WILL BE 
TURNING 74 ON SUNDAY.\r\n\r\nSO ONE GENERATION AGO WAS BORN IN 
SEGREGATION. SO WE DON'T HAVE TO LOOK VERY FAR AT HOW FAR WE HAVE COME 
AND HOW MUCH FURTHER WE HAVE YET TO GO. I'M THANKFUL THAT MY PARENTS 
RAISED ME ON MAUI TO BE HERE AND TO COME BACK TO HAWAI'I TO SERVE. I 
STAND IN MY ROLE AS PRESIDENT OF THE AFRICAN AMERICAN LAWYERS 
ASSOCIATION. I WAS ALSO ELECTED PRESIDENT OF THE MAUI COUNTY BAR 
ASSOCIATION AND DURING MY TERM I WAS THE FIRST BLACK PRESIDENT TO SERVE 
THERE. DURING MY TERM AS PRESIDENT OF AFRICAN AMERICAN LAWYERS 
ASSOCIATION, I'M REALLY PROUD WHAT OUR BAR HAS DONE. WE HAVE SEEN JUDGE 
BOWERS TO BE SWORN IN AS FIRST BLACK FEMALE JUDGE TO SERVE IN HIGH HYPE 
AND U.S. DISTRICT JUDGE MICHAEL FERNANDEZ TO SERVE FOR THE U.S. DISTRICT 
COURT OF HAWAI'I AND JOURNALING MALLEY TO BE THE FIRST BLACK JUDGE TO 
SERVE ON THE FAMILY COURT AND LED BY INCREDIBLE LEADERS SUCH AS JUDGE 
SANDERSSON WHO WAS THE FIRST BLACK FEMALE JUDGE IN ALL OF HAWAI'I. I'M 
JUST REALLY PROUD OF WHEN WE HAVE COME AND HOW MUCH FURTHER WE HAVE TO 
GO.\r\n\r\nBEING A BLACK FEMALE HERE, RAISED ON MAUI, I AM LED BY 
INCREDIBLE PEOPLE, SUCH AS MY AUNTIE JILL, WHO HELPED RAISE ME TO TEACH 
ME LANGUAGE, CULTURE AND THINGS. AND WHO DECIDED TO GO TO HEAVEN WITHOUT 
LETTING ME KNOW ON THE ANNIVERSARY OF MY LAW FIRM. I WOULDN'T BE WHERE I 
AM WITHOUT PEOPLE LIKE HER, WHO RAISED ME IN CULTURE AND LANGUAGE. I MISS 
HER EVERY DAY. SORRY. I CARRY PICTURES OF HER WITH ME TO COURT. EVERY 
MORNING SHE WOULD TELL ME LESLIE GET OUT THERE AND MAKE MAUI A BETTER 
PLACE OR YELL AT ME IN 'OLELO HAWAI'I AND TALK ABOUT DIVERSITY, EQUITY, 
AND INCLUSION TO BE SWORN INTO THE BAR FOR THE STATE OF HAWAI'I, AND ALSO 
TO THE U.S. DISTRICT COURT FOR THE DISTRICT OF HAWAI'I. WE TALK ABOUT 
SOMEONE WHO CAN SEE MOM GO UP AGAINST INCREDIBLE ODDS.\r\n\r\nWE TALK 
ABOUT EQUITY, WE TALK ABOUT ENSURING THAT PEOPLE CAN HAVE A VOICE, AND 
THEY CAN HAVE A SEAT AT THE TABLE OR IF THERE IS NO SEAT AT THE TABLE -- 
YOU CAN BRING YOUR OWN SEAT. I'M REALLY PROUD OF THE THINGS THAT THE 
AFRICAN AMERICAN LAWYERS ASSOCIATION HAS BEEN ABLE TO DO. WE TOOK PART 
WITH THE PACE COMMISSION THAT WAS AUTHORIZED BY THE SUPREME COURT TO 
START THE FIRST MAUI NUI LAW AND JUSTICE ACADEMY. WE HAD PEOPLE LIKE 
MALIA IN HER SENIOR YEAR OF HIGH SCHOOL LAUNCHED A PROJECT FOR PEER 
EQUITY AND TO MAKE SURE THAT PEOPLE WITH HAD PRODUCTS THAT THEY NEEDED 
AND RAISED OVER 10,000 PRODUCTS. AND I WILL JUST CLOSE BY SAYING I'M 
REALLY THANKFUL FOR MY TRIBE, MY SQUAD, WHO ALLOWS ME TO DO WHAT WE DO 
WITH WORK RELATED IN PROVERBS 38 AND 9 AND WHEN WE HAVE DIVERSE 
BACKGROUNDS AND REPRESENTATION, IT ALLOWS ME ONE DAY I WAS WALKING TO 
COURT AN ONE LADY IN 10TH GRADE SAYS HEY WHAT YOU ARE DOING? I'M GOING TO 
COURT. I DIDN'T KNOW LADIES COULD BE ATTORNEYS.\r\n\r\nGO BACK AND TALK 
TO YOUR COLLEGE COUNSELOR. SO JUST BY BEING WHO WE ARE, JUST BY BEING WHO 
GOD INTENDED US TO BE WE OPEN THE DOORS FOR SO MANY PEOPLE. MOM, THANK 
YOU FOR OPENING DOORS FOR ME. THANK YOU FOR FIGHTING FOR ME. TO MY 
GRANDMOTHER MATTHEWS, THANK YOU SO MUCH AND TO AUNTY JILL, I WILL NEVER 
FORGET YOU AND LOVE YOU FOREVER AND CONTINUE TO MAKE MAUI A BETTER PLACE. 
>> THANK YOU, MS. MATHEWS.\r\n\r\nANY QUESTIONS, MEMBERS? IF NOT, THANK 
YOU VERY MUCH. >> CHAIR, THE NEXT TESTIFIER IS ROBIN GARRISON, TESTIFYING 
ON RESOLUTION 25-37 AND SHE WILL BE FOLLOWED BY RAINY DOC MATHEWS. >> 
ALOHA, COUNCIL MEMBERS. THANK YOU FOR HAVING ME I HAVE BEEN PROUDLY BLACK 
AND ON MAUI FOR 26 YEARS. I STARTED BY VOLUNTEERING WITH WOMEN HELPING 
WOMEN, GIVING SOME WOMEN THE FIRST LOVING TOUCH THEY HAVE HAD EVER IN 
THEIR LIVE AND VOLUNTEERED AT MALAMA RECOVERY, HELPING PREGNANT WOMEN WHO 
WERE RECOVERING FROM SUBJECT ABUSE, I HAVE BEEN A SEXUAL ASSAULT NURSE 
EXAMINERS, AND NOW A HOSPICE NURSE AND NOW I'M A STREET MEDICINE NURSE 
PRACTITIONER HELPING THE MOST VULNERABLE ON THE STREETS OF MAUI. A COUPLE 
OF YEARS AGO I MET A BLACK WOMEN ON INTERSTATE, HER NAME IS KAREN SCOTT 
FROM NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE IN THE WAKE OF THE DEVASTATING FIRE THAT 
ENGULFED LAHAINA IN AUGUST 2023 EVERY DAY HEROES EMERGED FROM THE ASHES 
AS SHINING BEACONS OF HOPE AND HEALING FOR THEIR COMMUNITY AND AUTO LONG 
THESE LOCAL HEROES STANDS AN EXTRAORDINARY HUMAN MIDWIFE COMMUNITY-BASED 
NURSE PRACTITIONER AND HOSPICE PALLIATIVE CARE NURSE ROBIN GARRISON, 
WHOSE DEDICATION KNOWS NO BOUNDS AT THE TRAVERSES THE STREETS AND BEACHES 
OFFERING SOLACE AND SUPPORT.\r\n\r\nSPENDING THE AFTERNOON WITH ROBIN

WAY, AND IS A WAY TO BREAK DOWN THE BARRIERS. I SAW THAT AS A BLACK WOMAN

HOMELAND SECURITY, WHEN I -- I KNEW I WAS BLACK. I FIGURED THEY MAY HAVE

THAT HAD BEEN -- THAT HAD BEEN LAUNCHED AT PEOPLE WITH DISABILITIES IN

MY WALKER.\r\n\r\nPEOPLE SUCH AS ME, THAT HAVE -- I GOT IT. THAT HAVE

THANK YOU, MADAM CHAIR. RESOLUTION 25-71 CELEBRATING FEBRUARY 2025 AS 
BLACK HISTORY MONTH IN THE COUNTY OF MAUI. WHEREAS, ON FEBRUARY 10, 1976 
PRESIDENT GERALD R. FORD ISSUED A MESSAGE IN THE OBSERVANCE OF BLACK 
HISTORY MONTH; AND WHEREAS, EVERY UNITED STATES PRESIDENT HAS SINCE 
DESIGNATED THE MONTH OF FEBRUARY AS BLACK HISTORY MONTH; AND WHEREAS, 
BLACK HISTORY MONTH IS AN ANNUAL CELEBRATION OF ACHIEVEMENTS BY AFRICAN 
AMERICANS AND THEIR CONTRIBUTIONS IN THE UNITED STATES HISTORY; AND 
WHEREAS, MANY AFRICAN AMERICANS GUIDED BY A SENSE OF JUSTICE AND 
COMMITMENT TO A BETTER WORLD HAVE WORKED FOR SOCIAL PROGRESS AND AGAINST 
RACISM TO ACHIEVE SUCCESS AND TO MAKE SIGNIFICANT CONTRIBUTIONS TO THE 
ECONOMIC, EDUCATIONAL, POLITICAL, ARTISTIC, ATHLETIC, LITERARY, 
SCIENTIFIC, AND TECHNOLOGICAL ADVANCEMENT OF THE UNITED STATES; AND 
WHEREAS, ON NOVEMBER 4, 2008 THE PEOPLE OF THE UNITED STATES ELECTED 
PRESIDENT BARACK OBAMA TO BE THE FIRST AFRICAN AMERICAN PRESIDENT OF THE 
UNITED STATES; AND WHEREAS, DURING HIS TENURE, PRESIDENT OBAMA BROUGHT 
GLOBAL RECOGNITION AND ADMIRATION FOR CULTURAL DIVERSITY TO HIS 
BIRTHPLACE, THE STATE OF HAWAI'I; AND WHEREAS, BLACK THE PEOPLE HAVE MADE 
COUNTLESS INVALUABLE CONTRIBUTIONS TO MANY PHASES OF HAWAII'S 
DEVELOPMENT; AND WHEREAS, THE FIRST BLACK PEOPLE ARRIVED IN THE HAWAIIAN 
ISLANDS IN THE EARLY 1800S AS DECKHANDS ON MERCHANT AND WHALING SHIPS 
COMING FROM AFRICA, THE CARIBBEAN AND UNITED STATES AND MANY BECAME 
SUCCESSFUL MUSICIANS, BUSINESS PERSONS AND RESPECTED GOVERNMENT 
OFFICIALS; AND WHEREAS, IN 1897 BLACK CITIZENS OF THE KINGDOM OF HAWAI'I 
JOINED KANAKA MAOLI IN THEIR FIGHT FOR LIBERATION BY SIGNING THE KU'E 
PETITION PROTESTING THE ANNEXATION OF THE KINGDOM OF HAWAI'I BY THE 
UNITED STATES; AND WHEREAS, A DECADE BEFORE THE UNITED STATES CIVIL WAR 
AND THE EMANCIPATION PROCLAMATION ARTICLE 12 OF THE KINGDOM OF HAWAI'I 
CONSTITUTION OF 1852 SAID SLAVERY SHALL UNDER NO CIRCUMSTANCES WHATEVER 
BE TOLERATED IN THE HAWAIIAN ISLANDS AND WHATEVER A SLAVE SHALL ENTER THE 
HAWAIIAN TERRITORY HE SHALL BE FREE AND NO PERSON WHO IMPORTS A SLAVE OR 
SLAVES INTO THE KING'S DOMINIONS SHALL EVER ENJOY ANY CIVIL OR POLITICAL 
RIGHTS IN THIS REALM, BUT INVOLUNTARY SERVITUDE FOR THE PUNISHMENT OF 
CRIME IS NOT ALLOWABLE ACCORDING TO LAW; AND WHEREAS, AMONG THE MANY 
BLACK PEOPLE WHO HAVE MADE UNPRECEDENTED ACHIEVEMENTS TO HAWAII'S 
COMMUNITY THROUGHOUT THE HISTORY ANTHONY D. ALLEN ADVISOR AND STEWARD TO 
KING KAMEHAMEHA I, WILLIAM F. CROCKETT, MEMBER OF THE BOARD OF 
REGISTRATION OF WAILUKU DEPUTY COUNTY ATTORNEY OF THE COUNTY OF MAUI, A

AND OLIVER AND GEORGE WASHINGTON HYATT, THE FIRST TWO BAND MASTERS OF THE

DENOUNCING THE VIOLENCE USED BY ALABAMA GOVERNMENTAL AUTHORITIES AGAINST 
CIVIL RIGHTS DEMONSTRATORS AND URGING HAWAII'S CONGRESSIONAL DELEGATION 
TO VOTE FOR SWIFT PASSAGE OF NEW VOTING RIGHTS LEGISLATION; AND WHEREAS, 
ON AUGUST 18, TO 20 THE COUNCIL ADOPTED RESOLUTION 20-115 TO RECOGNIZE 
JUNETEENTH IN MAUI COUNTY; AND WHEREAS, OUR BLACK COMMUNITY IN IS THE 
CURRENT MANIFESTATION OF THEIR ANCESTORS AND CONTINUING TO CONTRIBUTE TO 
THE BETTERMENT OF HAWAI'I AS LEADERS, INNOVATORS, ENTREPRENEURS, 
EDUCATORS, ATHLETES, ARTISTS, CULTURAL PRACTITIONERS, ACTIVISTS, 
ENVIRONMENTALISTS, HEALTH CARE PROFESSIONALS, SCIENTISTS, ATTORNEYS, AND 
POLICYMAKERS AND WHEREAS, RECOGNITION OF THE CONTRIBUTIONS OF BLACK 
PEOPLE AND THEIR CULTURE IN IMPORTANT TO THE PROMOTION AND AWARENESS OF 
HAWAII'S DIVERSE AND MULTI-CULTURAL SOCIETY; NOW, THERETO BE IT RESOLVED 
BY THE COUNCIL OF THE COUNTY OF MAUI: 1, THAT IS CELEBRATES FEBRUARY 2025 
AS BLACK HISTORY MONTH IN THE COUNTY OF MAUI; 2, THAT IT RECOGNIZES THE 
IMPORTANCE OF BLACK HISTORY MONTH AS AN OPPORTUNITY TO REFLECT ON THE 
COMPLEX HISTORY OF THE UNITED STATES WHILE REMAINING HOPEFUL AND 
CONFIDENT ABOUT THE PATH TOWARD; AND 3, THAT IS IT PROUD TO ACKNOWLEDGE 
ALL OF THE AFRICAN AMERICANS WHO HAVE PLAYED AN IMPORTANT ROLE IN MAKING 
OUR COUNTY, STATE AND NATION A BETTER PLACE TO LIVE AND GRATEFUL FOR 
THEIR CONTRIBUTION AND LEADERSHIP; AND 4, THAT CERTIFIED COPIES OF THIS

THE GENERATIONAL LANDOWNERS ON THE LAHAINA SHORELINE IN WAYS THAT THE 
COUNTY, OR THE STATE OR COUNTY CANNOT. THESE FOLKS ARE FACING DIFFICULT 
DECISION TO SELL THEIR 'AINA, BECAUSE THEY MAY NOT BE ABLE TO REBUILD 
WHAT WAS LOST IN THE FIRE BECAUSE OF SHORELINE STUFF. UNLIKE OTHER 
AGENCIES LAHAINA CLT CAN DEVELOP PERPETUAL STEWARDSHIP AGREEMENTS WITH 
THOSE GENERATION OWNERS. THIS WORKS A LOT OF DIFFERENT WAYS DEPENDING ON 
THE NEEDS, BUT THE GIST IS THAT THE LAHAINA CLT BUYS THE 'AINA AND GIVES 
THE FAMILY RESOURCES TO MOVE INLAND AND THEN WORKS WITH 'OHANA TO 
MAINTAIN A RELATIONSHIP TO THE LAND ALLOWING ACCESS CONTINUATION OF 
CULTURAL PRACTICES AND WILL RESTORE THOSE NEAR SHORE ECHO SYSTEM AND 
PUBLIC ACCESS AND BENEFITS TO THE WIDER COMMUNITY AS WELL. WE'RE NOT 
REINVENTING THE WHEEL HERE, BUT THANKFULLY WE'RE BUILDING ON THE WORK OF 
OUR PARTNERS THAT HAVE BEEN IN THIS PACE FOR MANY YEARS, INCLUDING OUR 
SISTER LAND TRUST IN KAUA'I, WHO DOES VERY SIMILAR WELCOME AND TAKING 
DECLINES FROM HILTS AND OTHER LAND TRUSTS WHO HAVE CULTURAL EASEMENTS ON 
'AINA ACROSS HAWAI'I. THE FAMILIES WE'RE IN CONVERSATION ARE DOING 
EVERYTHING THAT THEY CAN TO RETAIN OWNERSHIP.\r\n\r\nSELLING IS A LAST 
RESORT, BUT WE LEARNED THAT ONCE A FAMILY MAKES THE CHOICE, THE REALLY 
DIFFICULT CHOICE TO SELL, THINGS TEND TO MOVE QUICKLY AND THE SPEED OF 
INVESTOR-DRIVEN REAL ESTATE ALSO MOVES QUICKLY. SO LAHAINA CLT NEEDS TO 
BE READY TO MOVE, MAKE OFFERS AND SAVE 'AINA AT THE SAME SPEED IN ORDER 
TO MEET METE THE FAMILY'S NEEDS AND ENSURE THE PARCELS ARE STEWARDED IN 
WAYS THAT CONSIDERS SEA-LEVEL RISE AND COMMUNITY NEEDS, RATHER THAN 
PROFIT OR LUXURY HOMES, WHICH IS WHY THEY WOULD PROBABLY END UP IF WE 
CAN'T MAKE AN OFFER. SO GIVING US PRE-APPROVED PERMISSION TO USE THIS 
MONEY TO ACQUIRE LAND WOULD ALLOW US TO SERVE ALL THOSE NEEDS? >>
